[$merge-to-main](/Users/kww/.codex/worktrees/c651/skiddee/.agents/skills/merge-to-main/SKILL.md)
Thu May 14 15:32:28
<skill> <name>merge-to-main</name> <path>/Users/kww/.codex/worktrees/c651/skiddee/.agents/skills/merge-to-main/SKILL.md</path> --- name: merge-to-main description: >- Land the current branch on main without checking out main. Single-commit branches are cherry-picked; multi-commit branches use a `--no-ff` merge commit. If a cherry-pick hits conflicts, it's aborted and falls back to a merge. Use when the user says "merge to main", "merge into main", "land this branch", "ship it to main", or wants to get their feature branch onto main — especially in worktree-based workflows where main may be checked out elsewhere. Keeps local `main` in sync with `origin/main` and never lets them diverge. Also use after completing feature work when the user wants to merge and clean up. --- # Merge to Main Land the current feature branch on `main` via the worktree where main is checked out, then push the resulting `main` to `origin/main`. Preserves any pre-existing uncommitted work in the main worktree. Guarantees that after the operation, local `main` and `origin/main` are equal — never diverged. **Single-commit branches are cherry-picked**, not merged — keeps history linear when there's nothing to gain from a merge commit. **Multi-commit branches use a `--no-ff` merge commit.** If a cherry-pick hits conflicts, it's aborted and falls back to a merge so the conflict resolution lives inside the merge commit (which can be reverted as a unit). **Default: do not ask for confirmation.** The user invoked this skill intentionally — proceed immediately. There is exactly one exception, in step 4: stashing uncommitted work in another worktree where `main` is checked out. That touches the user's in-progress work outside the current directory and requires explicit confirmation. Cd-ing into another worktree without stashing does not require confirmation — proceed. ## Safety Rules - **Never** run destructive commands: `git reset --hard`, `git clean -fdx`, `git worktree remove`, `rm`/`mv` on repository paths. - **Never** edit files outside git workflows unless required for conflict resolution. - **Always** preserve pre-existing user uncommitted changes in the main worktree. - **Never** leave `main` and `origin/main` diverged. If they are already diverged when the skill starts, abort and tell the user — do not try to fix it automatically. - **Always** end with the shell back in the directory the user invoked the skill from. ## Procedure ### 1. Pre-flight checks - Confirm the current working tree is clean (`git status --porcelain`). If not: - **If the uncommitted changes were authored in the current conversation** (i.e. you wrote them this session), commit them on the feature branch without asking. Use a concise, conventional commit message derived from the diff. Then re-check cleanliness and proceed. - **Otherwise** (the changes pre-existed the conversation, or you can't confidently attribute them), ask the user whether to stash or commit first. - Identify the current branch: `git branch --show-current`. Refuse if already on `main`. - Capture `ORIGINAL_DIR=$(pwd)` so step 10 can return here. Record the current branch name as `FEATURE_BRANCH` and its tip commit. Count the commits the branch adds on top of `main`: ```bash git rev-list --count main..HEAD ``` - `1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=true`. Cherry-pick path. - `>1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=false`. Merge path. - `0` → nothing to land. Abort and report. ### 2. Build the merge commit message (merge path only) Skip this step if `SINGLE_COMMIT=true` — cherry-pick reuses the original commit message. If the cherry-pick later falls back to a merge (step 8), build the message at that point. Gather the commits being merged: ```bash git log main..HEAD --oneline ``` Write a merge commit message in this format: ``` Merge <short description of the change, under 50 chars> <2-4 sentence summary of what this branch does, derived from the commit log> ``` The first line starts with "Merge " followed by a concise description of what changed (not the branch name). Keep the first line under 50 characters total. Examples: - `Merge audio duration tracking for cost analysis` - `Merge fix for Terms of Use placeholder values` The body should describe the _purpose_ of the changes — what feature was added, what bug was fixed, what was refactored — not just list commit subjects. ### 3. Sync `main` with `origin/main` and classify divergence Update the remote ref and compare: ```bash git fetch origin main git rev-list --left-right --count main...origin/main ``` The output is two numbers, `LEFT RIGHT`, where `LEFT` is commits on `main` not in `origin/main` and `RIGHT` is the reverse. Branch on the result: - `0 0` → equal. No fast-forward needed. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `N 0` (main ahead) → local `main` already descends from `origin/main`. Merging on top of `main` keeps it a descendant. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `0 N` (origin/main ahead) → `origin/main` descends from local `main`. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=true`. Step 5 will fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` before the feature merge. - `N M` (both > 0) → **diverged**. Abort. Report both counts to the user and instruct them to reconcile (rebase or merge `main` onto `origin/main`) before re-running the skill. Do not attempt to fix this automatically. ### 4. Locate where main is checked out, with confirmation gates Run `git worktree list --porcelain` and parse the output to find which worktree has `branch refs/heads/main`. Step 1 already refused if the _current_ branch is `main`, so two cases remain: **Case A — main is not checked out in any worktree.** Run `git checkout main` in the current worktree. Set `P=$(pwd)`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=false`. No confirmation needed. Continue at step 5. **Case B — main is checked out in another worktree at path `P`.** Set `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=false`. Inspect that worktree's cleanliness: ```bash git -C P status --porcelain ``` - **Clean** (empty output): `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=false`. No confirmation needed. - **Dirty** (non-empty output): ask the user `Worktree at P has uncommitted changes. OK to stash them, cd into P, perform the merge, then pop the stash?` On confirm, run `git -C P stash push -u -m "merge-to-main-pre-merge"`, then `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=true`. If the user declines the stash confirmation, abort the skill and report that nothing was changed. ### 5. Fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` (if needed) If `FFWD_NEEDED=true`, you are now in a working tree on branch `main` (either the current worktree from Case A or the other worktree from Case B after `cd P`). Run: ```bash git merge --ff-only origin/main ``` If this fails (it shouldn't — step 3 confirmed origin/main descends from main), abort and surface the error. ### 6. Verify main Confirm the working tree is on branch main: ```bash git branch --show-current ``` Expected output: `main`. If not, abort and report. ### 7. Land the feature branch on main Branch on `SINGLE_COMMIT`: **Cherry-pick path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=true`): ```bash git cherry-pick FEATURE_BRANCH ``` If the cherry-pick succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=cherry-pick` and proceed to step 9. If the cherry-pick fails with conflicts, **abort and fall back to merge**: ```bash git cherry-pick --abort ``` Then build the merge commit message now (the format from step 2) and continue into the merge path below. Set `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`. **Merge path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=false`, or cherry-pick fell back): ```bash git merge --no-ff FEATURE_BRANCH -m "<merge commit message>" ``` If the merge succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=merge` and proceed to step 9. ### 8. Resolve merge conflicts (if any) Only reachable on the merge path. If the merge fails with conflicts: 1. Inspect conflicting files: `git diff --name-only --diff-filter=U` 2. For each conflicting file, read the file and resolve the conflict. **Preserve the intent of both sides** — the feature branch's changes and main's existing content. Don't drop either side just because the diff is awkward; if you're unsure how to reconcile, ask the user. 3. Stage resolved files: `git add <file>` 4. Complete the merge: `git commit --no-edit` Record that conflicts were resolved (`CONFLICTS_RESOLVED=true`). ### 9. Restore stashed changes (if applicable) If `STASH_USED=true`, you are still inside `P`. Pop the stash: ```bash git stash pop ``` If stash pop conflicts, resolve them while **prioritizing pre-existing user edits** — the user's in-progress work takes precedence over formatting or trivial changes from the merge. ### 10. Return to the original directory and branch Always end up where the user started. - If `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true` (Case B): `cd "$ORIGINAL_DIR"`. The user is now back in their feature-branch worktree, on `FEATURE_BRANCH`, untouched. - Else (`SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, Case A): `git checkout FEATURE_BRANCH` so the user is back on their feature branch in the current worktree. This step runs whether the merge succeeded, was aborted partway, or hit conflicts — the user must end up back where they started. ### 11. Push `main` to `origin/main` From the original directory (refs are shared across worktrees, so this works from anywhere in the repo) push the new tip of `main` to the remote: ```bash git push origin main ``` This should be a fast-forward on the remote — step 3 already verified local `main` was a descendant of `origin/main` at fetch time, and step 7 only added the cherry-picked commit or merge commit on top. If the push is rejected as non-fast- forward (someone pushed to `origin/main` between the fetch in step 3 and now), **do not force**. Abort and tell the user: local `main` is correct but the remote has moved; they need to fetch, fast-forward `main` to the new `origin/main`, and re-push (or re-run the skill on top of an empty feature branch to redo the merge). ### 12. Report results Output a summary: - **Landed via**: `cherry-pick` or `merge` (from `LANDED_VIA`). If `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`, note that the cherry-pick was attempted and aborted due to conflicts before the merge. - **Commit hash**: the cherry-picked commit hash, or the merge commit hash on main. - **Commit message**: the first line of the commit message. - **Fast-forwarded main first**: yes/no (from `FFWD_NEEDED`). - **Performed in**: `P` (path of the worktree where the operation ran). - **Stash used**: yes/no. - **Conflicts resolved**: yes/no (merge and/or stash pop). Cherry-pick conflicts that triggered the fallback don't count — they were aborted, not resolved. - **Pushed to origin/main**: yes/no (no only if the push was rejected and step 11 aborted). - **Returned to**: `$ORIGINAL_DIR` (always). - **Manual follow-up**: any remaining issues requiring user attention. - Remind the user they can delete this worktree now if they're done with it. </skill>

If they are already diverged when the skill starts, abort and tell the user — do not try to fix it automatically. - **Always** end with the shell back in the directory the user invoked the skill from. ## Procedure ### 1. Pre-flight checks - Confirm the current working tree is clean (`git status --porcelain`). If not: - **If the uncommitted changes were authored in the current conversation** (i.e. you wrote them this session), commit them on the feature branch without asking. Use a concise, conventional commit message derived from the diff. Then re-check cleanliness and proceed. - **Otherwise** (the changes pre-existed the conversation, or you can't confidently attribute them), ask the user whether to stash or commit first. - Identify the current branch: `git branch --show-current`. Refuse if already on `main`. - Capture `ORIGINAL_DIR=$(pwd)` so step 10 can return here. Record the current branch name as `FEATURE_BRANCH` and its tip commit. Count the commits the branch adds on top of `main`: ```bash git rev-list --count main..HEAD ``` - `1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=true`. Cherry-pick path. - `>1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=false`. Merge path. - `0` → nothing to land. Abort and report. ### 2. Build the merge commit message (merge path only) Skip this step if `SINGLE_COMMIT=true` — cherry-pick reuses the original commit message. If the cherry-pick later falls back to a merge (step 8), build the message at that point. Gather the commits being merged: ```bash git log main..HEAD --oneline ``` Write a merge commit message in this format: ``` Merge <short description of the change, under 50 chars> <2-4 sentence summary of what this branch does, derived from the commit log> ``` The first line starts with "Merge " followed by a concise description of what changed (not the branch name). Keep the first line under 50 characters total. Examples: - `Merge audio duration tracking for cost analysis` - `Merge fix for Terms of Use placeholder values` The body should describe the _purpose_ of the changes — what feature was added, what bug was fixed, what was refactored — not just list commit subjects. ### 3. Sync `main` with `origin/main` and classify divergence Update the remote ref and compare: ```bash git fetch origin main git rev-list --left-right --count main...origin/main ``` The output is two numbers, `LEFT RIGHT`, where `LEFT` is commits on `main` not in `origin/main` and `RIGHT` is the reverse. Branch on the result: - `0 0` → equal. No fast-forward needed. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `N 0` (main ahead) → local `main` already descends from `origin/main`. Merging on top of `main` keeps it a descendant. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `0 N` (origin/main ahead) → `origin/main` descends from local `main`. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=true`. Step 5 will fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` before the feature merge. - `N M` (both > 0) → **diverged**. Abort. Report both counts to the user and instruct them to reconcile (rebase or merge `main` onto `origin/main`) before re-running the skill. Do not attempt to fix this automatically. ### 4. Locate where main is checked out, with confirmation gates Run `git worktree list --porcelain` and parse the output to find which worktree has `branch refs/heads/main`. Step 1 already refused if the _current_ branch is `main`, so two cases remain: **Case A — main is not checked out in any worktree.** Run `git checkout main` in the current worktree. Set `P=$(pwd)`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=false`. No confirmation needed. Continue at step 5. **Case B — main is checked out in another worktree at path `P`.** Set `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=false`. Inspect that worktree's cleanliness: ```bash git -C P status --porcelain ``` - **Clean** (empty output): `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=false`. No confirmation needed. - **Dirty** (non-empty output): ask the user `Worktree at P has uncommitted changes. OK to stash them, cd into P, perform the merge, then pop the stash?` On confirm, run `git -C P stash push -u -m "merge-to-main-pre-merge"`, then `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=true`. If the user declines the stash confirmation, abort the skill and report that nothing was changed. ### 5. Fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` (if needed) If `FFWD_NEEDED=true`, you are now in a working tree on branch `main` (either the current worktree from Case A or the other worktree from Case B after `cd P`). Run: ```bash git merge --ff-only origin/main ``` If this fails (it shouldn't — step 3 confirmed origin/main descends from main), abort and surface the error. ### 6. Verify main Confirm the working tree is on branch main: ```bash git branch --show-current ``` Expected output: `main`. If not, abort and report. ### 7. Land the feature branch on main Branch on `SINGLE_COMMIT`: **Cherry-pick path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=true`): ```bash git cherry-pick FEATURE_BRANCH ``` If the cherry-pick succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=cherry-pick` and proceed to step 9. If the cherry-pick fails with conflicts, **abort and fall back to merge**: ```bash git cherry-pick --abort ``` Then build the merge commit message now (the format from step 2) and continue into the merge path below. Set `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`. **Merge path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=false`, or cherry-pick fell back): ```bash git merge --no-ff FEATURE_BRANCH -m "<merge commit message>" ``` If the merge succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=merge` and proceed to step 9. ### 8. Resolve merge conflicts (if any) Only reachable on the merge path. If the merge fails with conflicts: 1. Inspect conflicting files: `git diff --name-only --diff-filter=U` 2. For each conflicting file, read the file and resolve the conflict. **Preserve the intent of both sides** — the feature branch's changes and main's existing content. Don't drop either side just because the diff is awkward; if you're unsure how to reconcile, ask the user. 3. Stage resolved files: `git add <file>` 4. Complete the merge: `git commit --no-edit` Record that conflicts were resolved (`CONFLICTS_RESOLVED=true`). ### 9. Restore stashed changes (if applicable) If `STASH_USED=true`, you are still inside `P`. Pop the stash: ```bash git stash pop ``` If stash pop conflicts, resolve them while **prioritizing pre-existing user edits** — the user's in-progress work takes precedence over formatting or trivial changes from the merge. ### 10. Return to the original directory and branch Always end up where the user started. - If `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true` (Case B): `cd "$ORIGINAL_DIR"`. The user is now back in their feature-branch worktree, on `FEATURE_BRANCH`, untouched. - Else (`SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, Case A): `git checkout FEATURE_BRANCH` so the user is back on their feature branch in the current worktree. This step runs whether the merge succeeded, was aborted partway, or hit conflicts — the user must end up back where they started. ### 11. Push `main` to `origin/main` From the original directory (refs are shared across worktrees, so this works from anywhere in the repo) push the new tip of `main` to the remote: ```bash git push origin main ``` This should be a fast-forward on the remote — step 3 already verified local `main` was a descendant of `origin/main` at fetch time, and step 7 only added the cherry-picked commit or merge commit on top. If the push is rejected as non-fast- forward (someone pushed to `origin/main` between the fetch in step 3 and now), **do not force**. Abort and tell the user: local `main` is correct but the remote has moved; they need to fetch, fast-forward `main` to the new `origin/main`, and re-push (or re-run the skill on top of an empty feature branch to redo the merge). ### 12. Report results Output a summary: - **Landed via**: `cherry-pick` or `merge` (from `LANDED_VIA`). If `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`, note that the cherry-pick was attempted and aborted due to conflicts before the merge. - **Commit hash**: the cherry-picked commit hash, or the merge commit hash on main. - **Commit message**: the first line of the commit message. - **Fast-forwarded main first**: yes/no (from `FFWD_NEEDED`). - **Performed in**: `P` (path of the worktree where the operation ran). - **Stash used**: yes/no. - **Conflicts resolved**: yes/no (merge and/or stash pop). Cherry-pick conflicts that triggered the fallback don't count — they were aborted, not resolved. - **Pushed to origin/main**: yes/no (no only if the push was rejected and step 11 aborted). - **Returned to**: `$ORIGINAL_DIR` (always). - **Manual follow-up**: any remaining issues requiring user attention. - Remind the user they can delete this worktree now if they're done with it. </skill>

For example: ```typescript import { httpRouter } from "convex/server"; import { httpAction } from "./_generated/server"; const http = httpRouter(); http.route({ path: "/echo", method: "POST", handler: httpAction(async (ctx, req) => { const body = await req.bytes(); return new Response(body, { status: 200 }); }), }); ``` - HTTP endpoints are always registered at the exact path you specify in the `path` field. [$merge-to-main](/Users/kww/.codex/worktrees/c900/skiddee/.agents/skills/merge-to-main/SKILL.md)
Thu May 14 14:05:15
<skill> <name>merge-to-main</name> <path>/Users/kww/.codex/worktrees/c900/skiddee/.agents/skills/merge-to-main/SKILL.md</path> --- name: merge-to-main description: >- Land the current branch on main without checking out main. Single-commit branches are cherry-picked; multi-commit branches use a `--no-ff` merge commit. If a cherry-pick hits conflicts, it's aborted and falls back to a merge. Use when the user says "merge to main", "merge into main", "land this branch", "ship it to main", or wants to get their feature branch onto main — especially in worktree-based workflows where main may be checked out elsewhere. Keeps local `main` in sync with `origin/main` and never lets them diverge. Also use after completing feature work when the user wants to merge and clean up. --- # Merge to Main Land the current feature branch on `main` via the worktree where main is checked out, then push the resulting `main` to `origin/main`. Preserves any pre-existing uncommitted work in the main worktree. Guarantees that after the operation, local `main` and `origin/main` are equal — never diverged. **Single-commit branches are cherry-picked**, not merged — keeps history linear when there's nothing to gain from a merge commit. **Multi-commit branches use a `--no-ff` merge commit.** If a cherry-pick hits conflicts, it's aborted and falls back to a merge so the conflict resolution lives inside the merge commit (which can be reverted as a unit). **Default: do not ask for confirmation.** The user invoked this skill intentionally — proceed immediately. There is exactly one exception, in step 4: stashing uncommitted work in another worktree where `main` is checked out. That touches the user's in-progress work outside the current directory and requires explicit confirmation. Cd-ing into another worktree without stashing does not require confirmation — proceed. ## Safety Rules - **Never** run destructive commands: `git reset --hard`, `git clean -fdx`, `git worktree remove`, `rm`/`mv` on repository paths. - **Never** edit files outside git workflows unless required for conflict resolution. - **Always** preserve pre-existing user uncommitted changes in the main worktree. - **Never** leave `main` and `origin/main` diverged. If they are already diverged when the skill starts, abort and tell the user — do not try to fix it automatically. - **Always** end with the shell back in the directory the user invoked the skill from. ## Procedure ### 1. Pre-flight checks - Confirm the current working tree is clean (`git status --porcelain`). If not: - **If the uncommitted changes were authored in the current conversation** (i.e. you wrote them this session), commit them on the feature branch without asking. Use a concise, conventional commit message derived from the diff. Then re-check cleanliness and proceed. - **Otherwise** (the changes pre-existed the conversation, or you can't confidently attribute them), ask the user whether to stash or commit first. - Identify the current branch: `git branch --show-current`. Refuse if already on `main`. - Capture `ORIGINAL_DIR=$(pwd)` so step 10 can return here. Record the current branch name as `FEATURE_BRANCH` and its tip commit. Count the commits the branch adds on top of `main`: ```bash git rev-list --count main..HEAD ``` - `1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=true`. Cherry-pick path. - `>1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=false`. Merge path. - `0` → nothing to land. Abort and report. ### 2. Build the merge commit message (merge path only) Skip this step if `SINGLE_COMMIT=true` — cherry-pick reuses the original commit message. If the cherry-pick later falls back to a merge (step 8), build the message at that point. Gather the commits being merged: ```bash git log main..HEAD --oneline ``` Write a merge commit message in this format: ``` Merge <short description of the change, under 50 chars> <2-4 sentence summary of what this branch does, derived from the commit log> ``` The first line starts with "Merge " followed by a concise description of what changed (not the branch name). Keep the first line under 50 characters total. Examples: - `Merge audio duration tracking for cost analysis` - `Merge fix for Terms of Use placeholder values` The body should describe the _purpose_ of the changes — what feature was added, what bug was fixed, what was refactored — not just list commit subjects. ### 3. Sync `main` with `origin/main` and classify divergence Update the remote ref and compare: ```bash git fetch origin main git rev-list --left-right --count main...origin/main ``` The output is two numbers, `LEFT RIGHT`, where `LEFT` is commits on `main` not in `origin/main` and `RIGHT` is the reverse. Branch on the result: - `0 0` → equal. No fast-forward needed. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `N 0` (main ahead) → local `main` already descends from `origin/main`. Merging on top of `main` keeps it a descendant. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `0 N` (origin/main ahead) → `origin/main` descends from local `main`. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=true`. Step 5 will fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` before the feature merge. - `N M` (both > 0) → **diverged**. Abort. Report both counts to the user and instruct them to reconcile (rebase or merge `main` onto `origin/main`) before re-running the skill. Do not attempt to fix this automatically. ### 4. Locate where main is checked out, with confirmation gates Run `git worktree list --porcelain` and parse the output to find which worktree has `branch refs/heads/main`. Step 1 already refused if the _current_ branch is `main`, so two cases remain: **Case A — main is not checked out in any worktree.** Run `git checkout main` in the current worktree. Set `P=$(pwd)`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=false`. No confirmation needed. Continue at step 5. **Case B — main is checked out in another worktree at path `P`.** Set `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=false`. Inspect that worktree's cleanliness: ```bash git -C P status --porcelain ``` - **Clean** (empty output): `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=false`. No confirmation needed. - **Dirty** (non-empty output): ask the user `Worktree at P has uncommitted changes. OK to stash them, cd into P, perform the merge, then pop the stash?` On confirm, run `git -C P stash push -u -m "merge-to-main-pre-merge"`, then `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=true`. If the user declines the stash confirmation, abort the skill and report that nothing was changed. ### 5. Fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` (if needed) If `FFWD_NEEDED=true`, you are now in a working tree on branch `main` (either the current worktree from Case A or the other worktree from Case B after `cd P`). Run: ```bash git merge --ff-only origin/main ``` If this fails (it shouldn't — step 3 confirmed origin/main descends from main), abort and surface the error. ### 6. Verify main Confirm the working tree is on branch main: ```bash git branch --show-current ``` Expected output: `main`. If not, abort and report. ### 7. Land the feature branch on main Branch on `SINGLE_COMMIT`: **Cherry-pick path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=true`): ```bash git cherry-pick FEATURE_BRANCH ``` If the cherry-pick succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=cherry-pick` and proceed to step 9. If the cherry-pick fails with conflicts, **abort and fall back to merge**: ```bash git cherry-pick --abort ``` Then build the merge commit message now (the format from step 2) and continue into the merge path below. Set `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`. **Merge path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=false`, or cherry-pick fell back): ```bash git merge --no-ff FEATURE_BRANCH -m "<merge commit message>" ``` If the merge succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=merge` and proceed to step 9. ### 8. Resolve merge conflicts (if any) Only reachable on the merge path. If the merge fails with conflicts: 1. Inspect conflicting files: `git diff --name-only --diff-filter=U` 2. For each conflicting file, read the file and resolve the conflict. **Preserve the intent of both sides** — the feature branch's changes and main's existing content. Don't drop either side just because the diff is awkward; if you're unsure how to reconcile, ask the user. 3. Stage resolved files: `git add <file>` 4. Complete the merge: `git commit --no-edit` Record that conflicts were resolved (`CONFLICTS_RESOLVED=true`). ### 9. Restore stashed changes (if applicable) If `STASH_USED=true`, you are still inside `P`. Pop the stash: ```bash git stash pop ``` If stash pop conflicts, resolve them while **prioritizing pre-existing user edits** — the user's in-progress work takes precedence over formatting or trivial changes from the merge. ### 10. Return to the original directory and branch Always end up where the user started. - If `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true` (Case B): `cd "$ORIGINAL_DIR"`. The user is now back in their feature-branch worktree, on `FEATURE_BRANCH`, untouched. - Else (`SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, Case A): `git checkout FEATURE_BRANCH` so the user is back on their feature branch in the current worktree. This step runs whether the merge succeeded, was aborted partway, or hit conflicts — the user must end up back where they started. ### 11. Push `main` to `origin/main` From the original directory (refs are shared across worktrees, so this works from anywhere in the repo) push the new tip of `main` to the remote: ```bash git push origin main ``` This should be a fast-forward on the remote — step 3 already verified local `main` was a descendant of `origin/main` at fetch time, and step 7 only added the cherry-picked commit or merge commit on top. If the push is rejected as non-fast- forward (someone pushed to `origin/main` between the fetch in step 3 and now), **do not force**. Abort and tell the user: local `main` is correct but the remote has moved; they need to fetch, fast-forward `main` to the new `origin/main`, and re-push (or re-run the skill on top of an empty feature branch to redo the merge). ### 12. Report results Output a summary: - **Landed via**: `cherry-pick` or `merge` (from `LANDED_VIA`). If `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`, note that the cherry-pick was attempted and aborted due to conflicts before the merge. - **Commit hash**: the cherry-picked commit hash, or the merge commit hash on main. - **Commit message**: the first line of the commit message. - **Fast-forwarded main first**: yes/no (from `FFWD_NEEDED`). - **Performed in**: `P` (path of the worktree where the operation ran). - **Stash used**: yes/no. - **Conflicts resolved**: yes/no (merge and/or stash pop). Cherry-pick conflicts that triggered the fallback don't count — they were aborted, not resolved. - **Pushed to origin/main**: yes/no (no only if the push was rejected and step 11 aborted). - **Returned to**: `$ORIGINAL_DIR` (always). - **Manual follow-up**: any remaining issues requiring user attention. - Remind the user they can delete this worktree now if they're done with it. </skill>

Work Day Logic (5am Boundary) **Purpose**: Handle late-night work sessions that cross midnight. **Algorithm**: ```javascript function getWorkDay(timestamp) { workDay = new Date(timestamp) if (workDay.getHours() < 5) { workDay.setDate(workDay.getDate() - 1) // Previous day } return workDay.toISOString().split('T')[0] } ``` **Benefits**: - Late night coding (12am-4am) counts toward previous day - More accurate representation of actual work sessions - Handles developers' irregular schedules ### 5. Heatmap Interval Mapping **Purpose**: Visualize work patterns in 15-minute increments. **Algorithm**: ```javascript // 96 intervals = 24 hours * 4 quarters intervals = new Array(96).fill(0) // Map session to intervals (5am = hour 0) startMinutes = (startHour - 5 + 24) % 24 * 60 + startMinutes endMinutes = (endHour - 5 + 24) % 24 * 60 + endMinutes startInterval = floor(startMinutes / 15) endInterval = floor(endMinutes / 15) // Mark all intervals during session for (i = startInterval; i <= endInterval; i++) { intervals[i] += 1 // Count overlapping sessions } ``` ## Data Structures ### Core Types ```typescript interface ConversationMessage { timestamp: string; // ISO timestamp type: 'user' | 'assistant' | 'summary'; sessionId: string; // Conversation identifier message?: object; // Message content durationMs?: number; // Response generation time costUSD?: number; // API cost } interface WorkSession { startTime: Date; endTime: Date; estimatedHours: number; // Calculated work time messages: ConversationMessage[]; sessionId: string; } interface DailyStats { date: string; // YYYY-MM-DD (work day format) totalHours: number; // Capped at 16 hours max sessions: WorkSession[]; messageCount: number; } interface IntervalData { date: string; intervals: number[]; // 96 intervals (15-min each) sessions: WorkSession[]; } ``` ## File Processing ### JSONL Format Claude stores conversations as JSON Lines: ```json {"timestamp":"2025-06-22T10:30:00.000Z","type":"user","sessionId":"abc123",...} {"timestamp":"2025-06-22T10:30:15.000Z","type":"assistant","sessionId":"abc123",...} ``` ### File Accumulation - Drag multiple files across multiple operations - Deduplicates by filename - Shows file count and preview - Manual "Analyze" trigger for control ### Error Handling - Skips malformed JSON lines - Validates file extensions (.jsonl) - Graceful degradation for missing fields ## Visualizations ### 1. Daily Hours Bar Chart - X-axis: Dates in d/m format (compact) - Y-axis: Estimated work hours - Responsive design for mobile/desktop ### 2. Gap Distribution Histogram - Shows message gap patterns - Helps validate break threshold selection - 20 bins, capped at 2 hours max ### 3. Work Pattern Heatmap - Rows: Each work day (including empty days) - Columns: 15-minute intervals (5am-4am) - Color intensity: Session overlap count - Weekend highlighting (amber background) - Sticky headers for easy navigation - Tooltips show exact times and session counts ## User Interface ### File Upload ```html <div class="upload-zone"> <!-- Drag & drop or click to select --> <button id="uploadButton">Select Files</button> [108] tool exec_command result: Chunk ID: 6e08a4 Wall time: 0.0002 seconds Process exited with code 0 Original token count: 1384 Output: --- description: Analyze Codex chat logs to estimate daily work hours by ISO week argument-hint: [iso-week|date-range|since-days|path] --- Analyze local Codex activity and produce a practical work-hours report. <skill> <name>merge-to-main</name> <path>/Users/kww/.codex/worktrees/c900/skiddee/.agents/skills/merge-to-main/SKILL.md</path> --- name: merge-to-main description: >- Land the current branch on main without checking out main. Single-commit branches are cherry-picked; multi-commit branches use a `--no-ff` merge commit. If a cherry-pick hits conflicts, it's aborted and falls back to a merge. Use when the user says "merge to main", "merge into main", "land this branch", "ship it to main", or wants to get their feature branch onto main — especially in worktree-based workflows where main may be checked out elsewhere. Keeps local `main` in sync with `origin/main` and never lets them diverge. Also use after completing feature work when the user wants to merge and clean up. --- # Merge to Main Land the current feature branch on `main` via the worktree where main is checked out, then push the resulting `main` to `origin/main`. Preserves any pre-existing uncommitted work in the main worktree. Guarantees that after the operation, local `main` and `origin/main` are equal — never diverged. **Single-commit branches are cherry-picked**, not merged — keeps history linear when there's nothing to gain from a merge commit. **Multi-commit branches use a `--no-ff` merge commit.** If a cherry-pick hits conflicts, it's aborted and falls back to a merge so the conflict resolution lives inside the merge commit (which can be reverted as a unit). **Default: do not ask for confirmation.** The user invoked this skill intentionally — proceed immediately. There is exactly one exception, in step 4: stashing uncommitted work in another worktree where `main` is checked out. That touches the user's in-progress work outside the current directory and requires explicit confirmation. Cd-ing into another worktree without stashing does not require confirmation — proceed. ## Safety Rules - **Never** run destructive commands: `git reset --hard`, `git clean -fdx`, `git worktree remove`, `rm`/`mv` on repository paths. - **Never** edit files outside git workflows unless required for conflict resolution. - **Always** preserve pre-existing user uncommitted changes in the main worktree. - **Never** leave `main` and `origin/main` diverged. If they are already diverged when the skill starts, abort and tell the user — do not try to fix it automatically. - **Always** end with the shell back in the directory the user invoked the skill from. ## Procedure ### 1. Pre-flight checks - Confirm the current working tree is clean (`git status --porcelain`). If not: - **If the uncommitted changes were authored in the current conversation** (i.e. you wrote them this session), commit them on the feature branch without asking. Use a concise, conventional commit message derived from the diff. Then re-check cleanliness and proceed. - **Otherwise** (the changes pre-existed the conversation, or you can't confidently attribute them), ask the user whether to stash or commit first. - Identify the current branch: `git branch --show-current`. Refuse if already on `main`. - Capture `ORIGINAL_DIR=$(pwd)` so step 10 can return here. Record the current branch name as `FEATURE_BRANCH` and its tip commit. Count the commits the branch adds on top of `main`: ```bash git rev-list --count main..HEAD ``` - `1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=true`. Cherry-pick path. - `>1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=false`. Merge path. - `0` → nothing to land. Abort and report. ### 2. Build the merge commit message (merge path only) Skip this step if `SINGLE_COMMIT=true` — cherry-pick reuses the original commit message. If the cherry-pick later falls back to a merge (step 8), build the message at that point. Gather the commits being merged: ```bash git log main..HEAD --oneline ``` Write a merge commit message in this format: ``` Merge <short description of the change, under 50 chars> <2-4 sentence summary of what this branch does, derived from the commit log> ``` The first line starts with "Merge " followed by a concise description of what changed (not the branch name). Keep the first line under 50 characters total. Examples: - `Merge audio duration tracking for cost analysis` - `Merge fix for Terms of Use placeholder values` The body should describe the _purpose_ of the changes — what feature was added, what bug was fixed, what was refactored — not just list commit subjects. ### 3. Sync `main` with `origin/main` and classify divergence Update the remote ref and compare: ```bash git fetch origin main git rev-list --left-right --count main...origin/main ``` The output is two numbers, `LEFT RIGHT`, where `LEFT` is commits on `main` not in `origin/main` and `RIGHT` is the reverse. Branch on the result: - `0 0` → equal. No fast-forward needed. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `N 0` (main ahead) → local `main` already descends from `origin/main`. Merging on top of `main` keeps it a descendant. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `0 N` (origin/main ahead) → `origin/main` descends from local `main`. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=true`. Step 5 will fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` before the feature merge. - `N M` (both > 0) → **diverged**. Abort. Report both counts to the user and instruct them to reconcile (rebase or merge `main` onto `origin/main`) before re-running the skill. Do not attempt to fix this automatically. ### 4. Locate where main is checked out, with confirmation gates Run `git worktree list --porcelain` and parse the output to find which worktree has `branch refs/heads/main`. Step 1 already refused if the _current_ branch is `main`, so two cases remain: **Case A — main is not checked out in any worktree.** Run `git checkout main` in the current worktree. Set `P=$(pwd)`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=false`. No confirmation needed. Continue at step 5. **Case B — main is checked out in another worktree at path `P`.** Set `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=false`. Inspect that worktree's cleanliness: ```bash git -C P status --porcelain ``` - **Clean** (empty output): `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=false`. No confirmation needed. - **Dirty** (non-empty output): ask the user `Worktree at P has uncommitted changes. OK to stash them, cd into P, perform the merge, then pop the stash?` On confirm, run `git -C P stash push -u -m "merge-to-main-pre-merge"`, then `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=true`. If the user declines the stash confirmation, abort the skill and report that nothing was changed. ### 5. Fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` (if needed) If `FFWD_NEEDED=true`, you are now in a working tree on branch `main` (either the current worktree from Case A or the other worktree from Case B after `cd P`). Run: ```bash git merge --ff-only origin/main ``` If this fails (it shouldn't — step 3 confirmed origin/main descends from main), abort and surface the error. ### 6. Verify main Confirm the working tree is on branch main: ```bash git branch --show-current ``` Expected output: `main`. If not, abort and report. ### 7. Land the feature branch on main Branch on `SINGLE_COMMIT`: **Cherry-pick path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=true`): ```bash git cherry-pick FEATURE_BRANCH ``` If the cherry-pick succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=cherry-pick` and proceed to step 9. If the cherry-pick fails with conflicts, **abort and fall back to merge**: ```bash git cherry-pick --abort ``` Then build the merge commit message now (the format from step 2) and continue into the merge path below. Set `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`. **Merge path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=false`, or cherry-pick fell back): ```bash git merge --no-ff FEATURE_BRANCH -m "<merge commit message>" ``` If the merge succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=merge` and proceed to step 9. ### 8. Resolve merge conflicts (if any) Only reachable on the merge path. If the merge fails with conflicts: 1. Inspect conflicting files: `git diff --name-only --diff-filter=U` 2. For each conflicting file, read the file and resolve the conflict. **Preserve the intent of both sides** — the feature branch's changes and main's existing content. Don't drop either side just because the diff is awkward; if you're unsure how to reconcile, ask the user. 3. Stage resolved files: `git add <file>` 4. Complete the merge: `git commit --no-edit` Record that conflicts were resolved (`CONFLICTS_RESOLVED=true`). ### 9. Restore stashed changes (if applicable) If `STASH_USED=true`, you are still inside `P`. Pop the stash: ```bash git stash pop ``` If stash pop conflicts, resolve them while **prioritizing pre-existing user edits** — the user's in-progress work takes precedence over formatting or trivial changes from the merge. ### 10. Return to the original directory and branch Always end up where the user started. - If `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true` (Case B): `cd "$ORIGINAL_DIR"`. The user is now back in their feature-branch worktree, on `FEATURE_BRANCH`, untouched. - Else (`SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, Case A): `git checkout FEATURE_BRANCH` so the user is back on their feature branch in the current worktree. This step runs whether the merge succeeded, was aborted partway, or hit conflicts — the user must end up back where they started. ### 11. Push `main` to `origin/main` From the original directory (refs are shared across worktrees, so this works from anywhere in the repo) push the new tip of `main` to the remote: ```bash git push origin main ``` This should be a fast-forward on the remote — step 3 already verified local `main` was a descendant of `origin/main` at fetch time, and step 7 only added the cherry-picked commit or merge commit on top. If the push is rejected as non-fast- forward (someone pushed to `origin/main` between the fetch in step 3 and now), **do not force**. Abort and tell the user: local `main` is correct but the remote has moved; they need to fetch, fast-forward `main` to the new `origin/main`, and re-push (or re-run the skill on top of an empty feature branch to redo the merge). ### 12. Report results Output a summary: - **Landed via**: `cherry-pick` or `merge` (from `LANDED_VIA`). If `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`, note that the cherry-pick was attempted and aborted due to conflicts before the merge. - **Commit hash**: the cherry-picked commit hash, or the merge commit hash on main. - **Commit message**: the first line of the commit message. - **Fast-forwarded main first**: yes/no (from `FFWD_NEEDED`). - **Performed in**: `P` (path of the worktree where the operation ran). - **Stash used**: yes/no. - **Conflicts resolved**: yes/no (merge and/or stash pop). Cherry-pick conflicts that triggered the fallback don't count — they were aborted, not resolved. - **Pushed to origin/main**: yes/no (no only if the push was rejected and step 11 aborted). - **Returned to**: `$ORIGINAL_DIR` (always). - **Manual follow-up**: any remaining issues requiring user attention. - Remind the user they can delete this worktree now if they're done with it. </skill>

<skill> <name>merge-to-main</name> <path>/Users/kww/.codex/worktrees/c651/skiddee/.agents/skills/merge-to-main/SKILL.md</path> --- name: merge-to-main description: >- Land the current branch on main without checking out main. Single-commit branches are cherry-picked; multi-commit branches use a `--no-ff` merge commit. If a cherry-pick hits conflicts, it's aborted and falls back to a merge. Use when the user says "merge to main", "merge into main", "land this branch", "ship it to main", or wants to get their feature branch onto main — especially in worktree-based workflows where main may be checked out elsewhere. Keeps local `main` in sync with `origin/main` and never lets them diverge. Also use after completing feature work when the user wants to merge and clean up. --- # Merge to Main Land the current feature branch on `main` via the worktree where main is checked out, then push the resulting `main` to `origin/main`. Preserves any pre-existing uncommitted work in the main worktree. Guarantees that after the operation, local `main` and `origin/main` are equal — never diverged. **Single-commit branches are cherry-picked**, not merged — keeps history linear when there's nothing to gain from a merge commit. **Multi-commit branches use a `--no-ff` merge commit.** If a cherry-pick hits conflicts, it's aborted and falls back to a merge so the conflict resolution lives inside the merge commit (which can be reverted as a unit). **Default: do not ask for confirmation.** The user invoked this skill intentionally — proceed immediately. There is exactly one exception, in step 4: stashing uncommitted work in another worktree where `main` is checked out. That touches the user's in-progress work outside the current directory and requires explicit confirmation. Cd-ing into another worktree without stashing does not require confirmation — proceed. ## Safety Rules - **Never** run destructive commands: `git reset --hard`, `git clean -fdx`, `git worktree remove`, `rm`/`mv` on repository paths. - **Never** edit files outside git workflows unless required for conflict resolution. - **Always** preserve pre-existing user uncommitted changes in the main worktree. - **Never** leave `main` and `origin/main` diverged. If they are already diverged when the skill starts, abort and tell the user — do not try to fix it automatically. - **Always** end with the shell back in the directory the user invoked the skill from. ## Procedure ### 1. Pre-flight checks - Confirm the current working tree is clean (`git status --porcelain`). If not: - **If the uncommitted changes were authored in the current conversation** (i.e. you wrote them this session), commit them on the feature branch without asking. Use a concise, conventional commit message derived from the diff. Then re-check cleanliness and proceed. - **Otherwise** (the changes pre-existed the conversation, or you can't confidently attribute them), ask the user whether to stash or commit first. - Identify the current branch: `git branch --show-current`. Refuse if already on `main`. - Capture `ORIGINAL_DIR=$(pwd)` so step 10 can return here. Record the current branch name as `FEATURE_BRANCH` and its tip commit. Count the commits the branch adds on top of `main`: ```bash git rev-list --count main..HEAD ``` - `1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=true`. Cherry-pick path. - `>1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=false`. Merge path. - `0` → nothing to land. Abort and report. ### 2. Build the merge commit message (merge path only) Skip this step if `SINGLE_COMMIT=true` — cherry-pick reuses the original commit message. If the cherry-pick later falls back to a merge (step 8), build the message at that point. Gather the commits being merged: ```bash git log main..HEAD --oneline ``` Write a merge commit message in this format: ``` Merge <short description of the change, under 50 chars> <2-4 sentence summary of what this branch does, derived from the commit log> ``` The first line starts with "Merge " followed by a concise description of what changed (not the branch name). Keep the first line under 50 characters total. Examples: - `Merge audio duration tracking for cost analysis` - `Merge fix for Terms of Use placeholder values` The body should describe the _purpose_ of the changes — what feature was added, what bug was fixed, what was refactored — not just list commit subjects. ### 3. Sync `main` with `origin/main` and classify divergence Update the remote ref and compare: ```bash git fetch origin main git rev-list --left-right --count main...origin/main ``` The output is two numbers, `LEFT RIGHT`, where `LEFT` is commits on `main` not in `origin/main` and `RIGHT` is the reverse. Branch on the result: - `0 0` → equal. No fast-forward needed. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `N 0` (main ahead) → local `main` already descends from `origin/main`. Merging on top of `main` keeps it a descendant. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `0 N` (origin/main ahead) → `origin/main` descends from local `main`. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=true`. Step 5 will fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` before the feature merge. - `N M` (both > 0) → **diverged**. Abort. Report both counts to the user and instruct them to reconcile (rebase or merge `main` onto `origin/main`) before re-running the skill. Do not attempt to fix this automatically. ### 4. Locate where main is checked out, with confirmation gates Run `git worktree list --porcelain` and parse the output to find which worktree has `branch refs/heads/main`. Step 1 already refused if the _current_ branch is `main`, so two cases remain: **Case A — main is not checked out in any worktree.** Run `git checkout main` in the current worktree. Set `P=$(pwd)`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=false`. No confirmation needed. Continue at step 5. **Case B — main is checked out in another worktree at path `P`.** Set `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=false`. Inspect that worktree's cleanliness: ```bash git -C P status --porcelain ``` - **Clean** (empty output): `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=false`. No confirmation needed. - **Dirty** (non-empty output): ask the user `Worktree at P has uncommitted changes. OK to stash them, cd into P, perform the merge, then pop the stash?` On confirm, run `git -C P stash push -u -m "merge-to-main-pre-merge"`, then `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=true`. If the user declines the stash confirmation, abort the skill and report that nothing was changed. ### 5. Fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` (if needed) If `FFWD_NEEDED=true`, you are now in a working tree on branch `main` (either the current worktree from Case A or the other worktree from Case B after `cd P`). Run: ```bash git merge --ff-only origin/main ``` If this fails (it shouldn't — step 3 confirmed origin/main descends from main), abort and surface the error. ### 6. Verify main Confirm the working tree is on branch main: ```bash git branch --show-current ``` Expected output: `main`. If not, abort and report. ### 7. Land the feature branch on main Branch on `SINGLE_COMMIT`: **Cherry-pick path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=true`): ```bash git cherry-pick FEATURE_BRANCH ``` If the cherry-pick succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=cherry-pick` and proceed to step 9. If the cherry-pick fails with conflicts, **abort and fall back to merge**: ```bash git cherry-pick --abort ``` Then build the merge commit message now (the format from step 2) and continue into the merge path below. Set `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`. **Merge path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=false`, or cherry-pick fell back): ```bash git merge --no-ff FEATURE_BRANCH -m "<merge commit message>" ``` If the merge succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=merge` and proceed to step 9. ### 8. Resolve merge conflicts (if any) Only reachable on the merge path. If the merge fails with conflicts: 1. Inspect conflicting files: `git diff --name-only --diff-filter=U` 2. For each conflicting file, read the file and resolve the conflict. **Preserve the intent of both sides** — the feature branch's changes and main's existing content. Don't drop either side just because the diff is awkward; if you're unsure how to reconcile, ask the user. 3. Stage resolved files: `git add <file>` 4. Complete the merge: `git commit --no-edit` Record that conflicts were resolved (`CONFLICTS_RESOLVED=true`). ### 9. Restore stashed changes (if applicable) If `STASH_USED=true`, you are still inside `P`. Pop the stash: ```bash git stash pop ``` If stash pop conflicts, resolve them while **prioritizing pre-existing user edits** — the user's in-progress work takes precedence over formatting or trivial changes from the merge. ### 10. Return to the original directory and branch Always end up where the user started. - If `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true` (Case B): `cd "$ORIGINAL_DIR"`. The user is now back in their feature-branch worktree, on `FEATURE_BRANCH`, untouched. - Else (`SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, Case A): `git checkout FEATURE_BRANCH` so the user is back on their feature branch in the current worktree. This step runs whether the merge succeeded, was aborted partway, or hit conflicts — the user must end up back where they started. ### 11. Push `main` to `origin/main` From the original directory (refs are shared across worktrees, so this works from anywhere in the repo) push the new tip of `main` to the remote: ```bash git push origin main ``` This should be a fast-forward on the remote — step 3 already verified local `main` was a descendant of `origin/main` at fetch time, and step 7 only added the cherry-picked commit or merge commit on top. If the push is rejected as non-fast- forward (someone pushed to `origin/main` between the fetch in step 3 and now), **do not force**. Abort and tell the user: local `main` is correct but the remote has moved; they need to fetch, fast-forward `main` to the new `origin/main`, and re-push (or re-run the skill on top of an empty feature branch to redo the merge). ### 12. Report results Output a summary: - **Landed via**: `cherry-pick` or `merge` (from `LANDED_VIA`). If `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`, note that the cherry-pick was attempted and aborted due to conflicts before the merge. - **Commit hash**: the cherry-picked commit hash, or the merge commit hash on main. - **Commit message**: the first line of the commit message. - **Fast-forwarded main first**: yes/no (from `FFWD_NEEDED`). - **Performed in**: `P` (path of the worktree where the operation ran). - **Stash used**: yes/no. - **Conflicts resolved**: yes/no (merge and/or stash pop). Cherry-pick conflicts that triggered the fallback don't count — they were aborted, not resolved. - **Pushed to origin/main**: yes/no (no only if the push was rejected and step 11 aborted). - **Returned to**: `$ORIGINAL_DIR` (always). - **Manual follow-up**: any remaining issues requiring user attention. - Remind the user they can delete this worktree now if they're done with it. </skill>

<skill> <name>merge-to-main</name> <path>/Users/kww/.codex/worktrees/c651/skiddee/.agents/skills/merge-to-main/SKILL.md</path> --- name: merge-to-main description: >- Land the current branch on main without checking out main. Single-commit branches are cherry-picked; multi-commit branches use a `--no-ff` merge commit. If a cherry-pick hits conflicts, it's aborted and falls back to a merge. Use when the user says "merge to main", "merge into main", "land this branch", "ship it to main", or wants to get their feature branch onto main — especially in worktree-based workflows where main may be checked out elsewhere. Keeps local `main` in sync with `origin/main` and never lets them diverge. Also use after completing feature work when the user wants to merge and clean up. --- # Merge to Main Land the current feature branch on `main` via the worktree where main is checked out, then push the resulting `main` to `origin/main`. Preserves any pre-existing uncommitted work in the main worktree. Guarantees that after the operation, local `main` and `origin/main` are equal — never diverged. **Single-commit branches are cherry-picked**, not merged — keeps history linear when there's nothing to gain from a merge commit. **Multi-commit branches use a `--no-ff` merge commit.** If a cherry-pick hits conflicts, it's aborted and falls back to a merge so the conflict resolution lives inside the merge commit (which can be reverted as a unit). **Default: do not ask for confirmation.** The user invoked this skill intentionally — proceed immediately. There is exactly one exception, in step 4: stashing uncommitted work in another worktree where `main` is checked out. That touches the user's in-progress work outside the current directory and requires explicit confirmation. Cd-ing into another worktree without stashing does not require confirmation — proceed. ## Safety Rules - **Never** run destructive commands: `git reset --hard`, `git clean -fdx`, `git worktree remove`, `rm`/`mv` on repository paths. - **Never** edit files outside git workflows unless required for conflict resolution. - **Always** preserve pre-existing user uncommitted changes in the main worktree. - **Never** leave `main` and `origin/main` diverged. If they are already diverged when the skill starts, abort and tell the user — do not try to fix it automatically. - **Always** end with the shell back in the directory the user invoked the skill from. ## Procedure ### 1. Pre-flight checks - Confirm the current working tree is clean (`git status --porcelain`). If not: - **If the uncommitted changes were authored in the current conversation** (i.e. you wrote them this session), commit them on the feature branch without asking. Use a concise, conventional commit message derived from the diff. Then re-check cleanliness and proceed. - **Otherwise** (the changes pre-existed the conversation, or you can't confidently attribute them), ask the user whether to stash or commit first. - Identify the current branch: `git branch --show-current`. Refuse if already on `main`. - Capture `ORIGINAL_DIR=$(pwd)` so step 10 can return here. Record the current branch name as `FEATURE_BRANCH` and its tip commit. Count the commits the branch adds on top of `main`: ```bash git rev-list --count main..HEAD ``` - `1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=true`. Cherry-pick path. - `>1` → set `SINGLE_COMMIT=false`. Merge path. - `0` → nothing to land. Abort and report. ### 2. Build the merge commit message (merge path only) Skip this step if `SINGLE_COMMIT=true` — cherry-pick reuses the original commit message. If the cherry-pick later falls back to a merge (step 8), build the message at that point. Gather the commits being merged: ```bash git log main..HEAD --oneline ``` Write a merge commit message in this format: ``` Merge <short description of the change, under 50 chars> <2-4 sentence summary of what this branch does, derived from the commit log> ``` The first line starts with "Merge " followed by a concise description of what changed (not the branch name). Keep the first line under 50 characters total. Examples: - `Merge audio duration tracking for cost analysis` - `Merge fix for Terms of Use placeholder values` The body should describe the _purpose_ of the changes — what feature was added, what bug was fixed, what was refactored — not just list commit subjects. ### 3. Sync `main` with `origin/main` and classify divergence Update the remote ref and compare: ```bash git fetch origin main git rev-list --left-right --count main...origin/main ``` The output is two numbers, `LEFT RIGHT`, where `LEFT` is commits on `main` not in `origin/main` and `RIGHT` is the reverse. Branch on the result: - `0 0` → equal. No fast-forward needed. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `N 0` (main ahead) → local `main` already descends from `origin/main`. Merging on top of `main` keeps it a descendant. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=false` and proceed. - `0 N` (origin/main ahead) → `origin/main` descends from local `main`. Set `FFWD_NEEDED=true`. Step 5 will fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` before the feature merge. - `N M` (both > 0) → **diverged**. Abort. Report both counts to the user and instruct them to reconcile (rebase or merge `main` onto `origin/main`) before re-running the skill. Do not attempt to fix this automatically. ### 4. Locate where main is checked out, with confirmation gates Run `git worktree list --porcelain` and parse the output to find which worktree has `branch refs/heads/main`. Step 1 already refused if the _current_ branch is `main`, so two cases remain: **Case A — main is not checked out in any worktree.** Run `git checkout main` in the current worktree. Set `P=$(pwd)`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=false`. No confirmation needed. Continue at step 5. **Case B — main is checked out in another worktree at path `P`.** Set `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true`, `SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=false`. Inspect that worktree's cleanliness: ```bash git -C P status --porcelain ``` - **Clean** (empty output): `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=false`. No confirmation needed. - **Dirty** (non-empty output): ask the user `Worktree at P has uncommitted changes. OK to stash them, cd into P, perform the merge, then pop the stash?` On confirm, run `git -C P stash push -u -m "merge-to-main-pre-merge"`, then `cd P`. Set `STASH_USED=true`. If the user declines the stash confirmation, abort the skill and report that nothing was changed. ### 5. Fast-forward `main` to `origin/main` (if needed) If `FFWD_NEEDED=true`, you are now in a working tree on branch `main` (either the current worktree from Case A or the other worktree from Case B after `cd P`). Run: ```bash git merge --ff-only origin/main ``` If this fails (it shouldn't — step 3 confirmed origin/main descends from main), abort and surface the error. ### 6. Verify main Confirm the working tree is on branch main: ```bash git branch --show-current ``` Expected output: `main`. If not, abort and report. ### 7. Land the feature branch on main Branch on `SINGLE_COMMIT`: **Cherry-pick path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=true`): ```bash git cherry-pick FEATURE_BRANCH ``` If the cherry-pick succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=cherry-pick` and proceed to step 9. If the cherry-pick fails with conflicts, **abort and fall back to merge**: ```bash git cherry-pick --abort ``` Then build the merge commit message now (the format from step 2) and continue into the merge path below. Set `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`. **Merge path** (`SINGLE_COMMIT=false`, or cherry-pick fell back): ```bash git merge --no-ff FEATURE_BRANCH -m "<merge commit message>" ``` If the merge succeeds, set `LANDED_VIA=merge` and proceed to step 9. ### 8. Resolve merge conflicts (if any) Only reachable on the merge path. If the merge fails with conflicts: 1. Inspect conflicting files: `git diff --name-only --diff-filter=U` 2. For each conflicting file, read the file and resolve the conflict. **Preserve the intent of both sides** — the feature branch's changes and main's existing content. Don't drop either side just because the diff is awkward; if you're unsure how to reconcile, ask the user. 3. Stage resolved files: `git add <file>` 4. Complete the merge: `git commit --no-edit` Record that conflicts were resolved (`CONFLICTS_RESOLVED=true`). ### 9. Restore stashed changes (if applicable) If `STASH_USED=true`, you are still inside `P`. Pop the stash: ```bash git stash pop ``` If stash pop conflicts, resolve them while **prioritizing pre-existing user edits** — the user's in-progress work takes precedence over formatting or trivial changes from the merge. ### 10. Return to the original directory and branch Always end up where the user started. - If `MOVED_TO_OTHER_WORKTREE=true` (Case B): `cd "$ORIGINAL_DIR"`. The user is now back in their feature-branch worktree, on `FEATURE_BRANCH`, untouched. - Else (`SWITCHED_TO_MAIN=true`, Case A): `git checkout FEATURE_BRANCH` so the user is back on their feature branch in the current worktree. This step runs whether the merge succeeded, was aborted partway, or hit conflicts — the user must end up back where they started. ### 11. Push `main` to `origin/main` From the original directory (refs are shared across worktrees, so this works from anywhere in the repo) push the new tip of `main` to the remote: ```bash git push origin main ``` This should be a fast-forward on the remote — step 3 already verified local `main` was a descendant of `origin/main` at fetch time, and step 7 only added the cherry-picked commit or merge commit on top. If the push is rejected as non-fast- forward (someone pushed to `origin/main` between the fetch in step 3 and now), **do not force**. Abort and tell the user: local `main` is correct but the remote has moved; they need to fetch, fast-forward `main` to the new `origin/main`, and re-push (or re-run the skill on top of an empty feature branch to redo the merge). ### 12. Report results Output a summary: - **Landed via**: `cherry-pick` or `merge` (from `LANDED_VIA`). If `FELL_BACK_FROM_CHERRY_PICK=true`, note that the cherry-pick was attempted and aborted due to conflicts before the merge. - **Commit hash**: the cherry-picked commit hash, or the merge commit hash on main. - **Commit message**: the first line of the commit message. - **Fast-forwarded main first**: yes/no (from `FFWD_NEEDED`). - **Performed in**: `P` (path of the worktree where the operation ran). - **Stash used**: yes/no. - **Conflicts resolved**: yes/no (merge and/or stash pop). Cherry-pick conflicts that triggered the fallback don't count — they were aborted, not resolved. - **Pushed to origin/main**: yes/no (no only if the push was rejected and step 11 aborted). - **Returned to**: `$ORIGINAL_DIR` (always). - **Manual follow-up**: any remaining issues requiring user attention. - Remind the user they can delete this worktree now if they're done with it. </skill>

Works with accessibility-tree snapshots and compact `@eN` element refs. State (open tab, viewport, cookies) persists across invocations until you `close` or the process is torn down by inactivity. ## Start here — load the canonical guide from the CLI This file is a pragmatic supplement, not the authoritative usage guide. Before running non-trivial commands, load the workflow content the CLI ships with (always matches the installed version): ```bash agent-browser skills get core # workflows, common patterns, troubleshooting agent-browser skills get core --full # include full command reference and templates ``` Specialized skills for tasks outside plain web pages: ```bash agent-browser skills get electron # Electron desktop apps (VS Code, Slack, Discord, Figma, ...) agent-browser skills get slack # Slack workspace automation agent-browser skills get dogfood # Exploratory testing / QA / bug hunts agent-browser skills get ver<truncated omitted_approx_tokens="925" /> if (r.right > window.innerWidth + 5) { out.push({ d, tag: el.tagName, cls: (typeof el.className === 'string' ? el.className : '').slice(0, 100), l: r.left, r: r.right, }); } for (const c of el.children) walk(c, d + 1); }; walk(main, 0); return out.slice(0, 20); })()" ``` The shallowest offender (lowest `d`) is usually the culprit — often a `grid-cols-[...]`, a fixed-width container, or a table without a mobile strategy. ### Reaching deep UI state For multi-step flows (login → select item → open modal), don't script it all in one bash line. Do one command, snapshot, read the result, pick the next ref. Refs change between snapshots, so chaining pre-computed refs fails. If login is OAuth via an emulator (Skiddee uses a Google OAuth emulator), expect an extra sleep + snapshot between redirect hops. ## Useful commands beyond the basics - `agent-browser reload` — hard reload (re-applies viewport) - `agent-browser get url` — current URL (sanity-check after clicks) - `agent-browser get text @e4` — extract text from an element - `agent-browser fill @e6 "value"` — clear + type into input - `agent-browser press Enter` — submit a form - `agent-browser scroll down 500` — scroll by pixels - `agent-browser close` — close the browser (use sparingly; losing state means re-setting viewport and re-logging-in) Full list: `agent-browser --help`. ## Gotchas - **Ref `@e1` collision**: skipping `@` gives a cryptic `Unknown ref` — always prefix. - **`set device` drift**: if a later `eval "window.innerWidth"` returns a surprise like 543 or 1280, you lost the device setting — re-apply `set viewport`. - **`open` with query params**: quote the whole URL; `&` in unquoted URLs backgrounds the shell. - **Screenshots of `position: fixed` TanStack devtools**: the dev tools badge overlays the bottom-right corner. Either dismiss it (`click @eN` on the badge) or crop after the fact. Chrome/Chromium via CDP, no Playwright or Puppeteer dependency. Accessibility-tree snapshots with compact `@eN` refs let agents interact with pages in ~200-400 tokens instead of parsing raw HTML. Most normal web tasks (navigate, read, click, fill, extract, screenshot) are covered here. Load a specialized skill when the task falls outside browser web pages — see [When to load another skill](#when-to-load-another-skill). ## The core loop ```bash agent-browser open <url> # 1. Open a page agent-browser snapshot -i # 2. See what's on it (interactive elements only) agent-browser click @e3 # 3. Act on refs from the snapshot agent-browser snapshot -i # 4. Re-snapshot after any page change ``` Refs (`@e1`, `@e2`, ...) are assigned fresh on every snapshot. They become **stale the moment the page changes** — after clicks that navigate, form submits, dynamic re-renders, dialog opens. Always re-snapshot before your next ref interaction. ## Quickstart ```bash # Install once npm i -g agent-browser && agent-browser install # Take a screenshot of a page agent-browser open https://example.com agent-browser scre<truncated omitted_approx_tokens="3019" />ave`/`state load` so your session survives browser restarts. See [references/session-management.md](references/session-management.md) and [references/authentication.md](references/authentication.md). ## Global flags worth knowing ```bash --session <name> # isolated browser session --json # JSON output (for machine parsing) --headed # show the window (default is headless) --auto-connect # connect to an already-running Chrome --cdp <port> # connect to a specific CDP port --profile <name|path> # use a Chrome profile (login state survives) --headers <json> # HTTP headers scoped to the URL's origin --proxy <url> # proxy server --state <path> # load saved auth state from JSON --session-name <name> # auto-save/restore session state by name ``` ## When to load another skill - **Electron desktop app** (VS Code, Slack desktop, Discord, Figma, etc.): `agent-browser skills get electron` - **Slack workspace automation**: `agent-browser skills get slack` - **Exploratory testing / QA / bug hunts**: `agent-browser skills get dogfood` - **Vercel Sandbox microVMs**: `agent-browser skills get vercel-sandbox` - **AWS Bedrock AgentCore cloud browser**: `agent-browser skills get agentcore` ## Full reference Everything covered here plus the complete command/flag/env listing: ```bash agent-browser skills get core --full ``` That pulls in: - For iteration, use `pnpm dev` against your personal dev deployment — same as today. `pnpm preview` is for sharing a working URL or validating the branch state, not for inner-loop development. This skill should be used when users want to create a new skill (or update an existing skill) that extends Codex's capabilities with specialized knowledge, workflows, or tool integrations. metadata: short-description: Create or update a skill --- # Skill Creator This skill provides guidance for creating effective skills. ## About Skills Skills are modular, self-contained folders that extend Codex's capabilities by providing specialized knowledge, workflows, and tools. Think of them as "onboarding guides" for specific domains or tasks—they transform Codex from a general-purpose agent into a specialized agent equipped with procedural knowledge that no model can fully possess. ### What Skills Provide 1. Specialized workflows - Multi-step procedures for specific domains 2. Tool integrations - Instructions for working with specific file formats or APIs 3. Domain expertise - Company-specific knowledge, schemas, business logic 4. Bundled resources - Scripts, references, and assets for complex and repetitive tasks ## Core Principles ### Concise is Key The context window is a public good. Skills share the context window with everything else Codex needs: system prompt, conversation history, other Skills' metadata, and the actual user request. **Default assumption: Codex is already very smart.** Only add context Codex doesn't already have. Challenge each piece of information: "Does Codex really need this explanation?" and "Does this paragraph justify its token cost?" Prefer concise examples over verbose explanations. ### Set Appropriate Degrees of Freedom Match the level of specificity to the task's fragility and variability: **High freedom (text-based instructions)**: Use when multiple approaches are valid, decisions depend on context, or heuristics guide the ap<truncated omitted_approx_tokens="1635" />als and under 500 lines to minimize context bloat. Split content into separate files when approaching this limit. When splitting out content into other files, it is very important to reference them from SKILL.md and describe clearly when to read them, to ensure the reader of the skill knows they exist and when to use them. **Key principle:** When a skill supports multiple variations, frameworks, or options, keep only the core workflow and selection guidance in SKILL.md. Move variant-specific details (patterns, examples, configuration) into separate reference files. **Pattern 1: High-level guide with references** ```markdown # PDF Processing ## Quick start Extract text with pdfplumber: [code example] ## Advanced features - **Form filling**: See [FORMS.md](FORMS.md) for complete guide - **API reference**: See [REFERENCE.md](REFERENCE.md) for all methods - **Examples**: See [EXAMPLES.md](EXAMPLES.md) for common patterns ``` Codex loads FORMS.md, REFERENCE.md, or EXAMPLES.md only when needed. **Pattern 2: Domain-specific organization** For Skills with multiple domains, organize content by domain to avoid loading irrelevant context: ``` bigquery-skill/ ├── SKILL.md (overview and navigation) └── reference/ ├── finance.md (revenue, billing metrics) ├── sales.md (opportunities, pipeline) ├── product.md (API usage, features) └── marketing.md (campaigns, attribution) ``` When a user asks about sales metrics, Codex only reads sales.md. Similarly, for skills supporting multiple frameworks or variants, organize by variant: ``` cloud-deploy/ ├── SKILL.md (workflow + provider selection) └── references/ ├── aws.md (AWS deployment patterns) ├── gcp.md (GCP deployment patterns) └── azure.md (Azure deployment patterns) ``` When the user chooses AWS, Codex only reads aws.md. **Pattern 3: Conditional details** Show basic content, link to advanced content: [44] assistant: I’m editing the preview scripts now. The key behavior is: branch name when available, explicit name when detached, no accidental shared `HEAD` preview cache.
